## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy TLS Certificate Validation Pipeline

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement TLS certificate validation. Identify: the abstract CertValidator interface, the DefaultCertValidator with X.509 chain verification, the SAN matcher for Subject Alternative Name matching (DNS, URI, email, IP), the ContextImpl managing TLS certificates and OCSP responses, and the OCSP response parsing and stapling support.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the TLS certificate validation pipeline in Envoy. Here's a summary of the findings:

## Summary

I've identified **all C++ source files** implementing TLS certificate validation in Envoy v1.31.2:

### **Core Components:**

1. **Abstract CertValidator Interface** (`source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h`)
   - Pure virtual base class defining certificate validation contract
   - Methods: `addClientValidationContext()`, `doVerifyCertChain()`, `initializeSslContexts()`

2. **DefaultCertValidator with X.509 Chain Verification** (`source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.*`)
   - Full X.509 certificate chain validation implementation
   - X509_STORE configuration with CA certificates and CRL support
   - Certificate pinning (SHA-256 hash and SPKI verification)
   - Hostname matching and expiration checking

3. **SAN Matcher for Subject Alternative Names** (`source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.*`)
   - Abstract `SanMatcher` interface and `StringSanMatcher` implementation
   - Support for DNS (with DNS matching semantics), URI, Email, IP, and OtherName types
   - Flexible string matching via exact, prefix, suffix, and regex patterns

4. **ContextImpl Managing TLS Certificates** (`source/common/tls/context_impl.*`)
   - Manages SSL_CTX instances and certificate chains
   - Coordinates with CertValidator during handshake
   - Stores certificate metadata in TlsContext structure

5. **ServerContextImpl Managing OCSP Stapling** (`source/common/tls/server_context_impl.*`)
   - Extends ContextImpl for server-side certificate selection
   - OCSP stapling decision logic based on client capabilities and policy
   - ClientHello callback for certificate and response selection

source/common/tls and consists of several key components working together to provide comprehensive X.509 certificate validation and OCSP stapling support.\\n\\n**Abstract Interface**: The CertValidator abstract class (source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h) defines the core interface with three critical methods: addClientValidationContext() to configure client certificate validation, doVerifyCertChain() to perform asynchronous or synchronous certificate chain verification, and initializeSslContexts() to initialize SSL contexts with verification modes and CA certificates. The ValidationResults struct captures validation status, detailed status, TLS alerts, and error details.\\n\\n**X.509 Chain Verification**: DefaultCertValidator (source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.h and default_validator.cc) implements the CertValidator interface with full X.509 chain validation. The initializeSslContexts() method loads CA certificates from PEM format into X509_STORE structures, configures X509_STORE_CTX with certificate chain verification flags (X509_V_FLAG_PARTIAL_CHAIN), enables CRL checking when configured, and supports expiration tolerance. The doVerifyCertChain() method performs actual chain verification using X509_verify_cert() and validates certificate properties including hostname matching, certificate pinning (SHA-256 hash and SPKI), and expiration dates.\\n\\n**Subject Alternative Name (SAN) Matching**: The SanMatcher abstract class and StringSanMatcher implementation (source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h and san_matcher.cc) handle SAN verification with support for multiple SAN types. The createStringSanMatcher() factory function maps protobuf SubjectAltNameMatcher configurations to StringSanMatcher instances supporting DNS (GEN_DNS with DNS matching semantics), URI (GEN_URI), Email (GEN_EMAIL), IP address (GEN_IPADD), and OtherName (GEN_OTHERNAME with custom OID) types. The match() method extracts GENERAL_NAME structures from X509 certificates and applies StringMatcher logic (exact, prefix, suffix, regex) to verify SAN fields.\\n\\n**TLS Context Management**: ContextImpl (source/common/tls/context_impl.h and context_impl.cc) manages SSL contexts, certificate chains, and invokes the cert_validator_. The TlsContext structure (in context_impl.h) stores per-certificate data including SSL_CTX, X509 certificate chain, file paths, OCSP responses, ECDSA indicators, must-staple flags, and private key method providers. ContextImpl::customVerifyCertChain() is a static callback triggered during TLS handshake that delegates to the CertValidator for certificate verification.\\n\\n**OCSP Response Stapling**: ServerContextImpl (source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h and server_context_impl.cc) extends ContextImpl to add OCSP stapling support during the TLS handshake. The findTlsContext() method selects the appropriate certificate context based on SNI and client capabilities. The ocspStapleAction() method determines whether to staple, omit, or fail based on certificate must-staple flags and OCSP staple policy (LENIENT_STAPLING, OPTIONAL, MUST_STAPLE). During the ClientHello callback in selectTlsContext(), the stapling action is applied via SSL_set_ocsp_response().\\n\\n**OCSP Response Parsing**: The Ocsp namespace (source/common/tls/ocsp/ocsp.h and ocsp.cc) provides RFC 6960-compliant OCSP response parsing. OcspResponse is the top-level structure containing OcspResponseStatus (Successful, MalformedRequest, InternalError, TryLater, SigRequired, Unauthorized) and a polymorphic Response object. BasicOcspResponse implements Response for the standard OCSP response type and contains ResponseData with SingleResponse elements. SingleResponse holds CertId (certificate serial number), thisUpdate, and nextUpdate timestamps to track response validity windows. OcspResponseWrapperImpl (implementing the OcspResponseWrapper interface from envoy/ssl/context.h) wraps parsed OCSP responses and provides validity checking via isExpired() (checks nextUpdate against current time) and secondsUntilExpiration() for response lifetime tracking.\\n\\n**ASN.1 Parsing Utilities**: Asn1OcspUtility (source/common/tls/ocsp/asn1_utility.h and asn1_utility.cc) provides RFC 6960 Appendix B ASN.1 parsing functions. The Asn1Utility base class provides parseInteger(), parseOid(), parseGeneralizedTime(), parseOctetString(), parseSequenceOf(), and parseOptional() template functions that use BoringSSL's CBS (crypto bytestring) API for DER parsing. OCSP-specific functions include parseOcspResponse() (top-level), parseResponseStatus() (ENUMERATED status), parseResponseBytes() (Response type dispatch), parseBasicOcspResponse() (BasicOcspResponse), parseResponseData() (multiple SingleResponse elements), parseSingleResponse(), and parseCertId(). OcspResponseWrapperImpl::matchesCertificate() verifies OCSP response applicability by comparing certificate serial numbers.\\n\\n**Certificate Validation Context Configuration**: CertificateValidationContextConfig (referenced throughout) provides configuration for trust chain verification mode, CA certificates/CRL, certificate pinning hashes, SAN matchers, and expiration tolerance settings. The factory pattern via CertValidatorFactory (source/common/tls/cert_validator/factory.h) enables pluggable validators like DefaultCertValidator, SPIFFEValidator, and PlatformBridgeCertValidator.\\n\\nThe complete validation flow: (1) Server/Client TLS context initialization calls initializeSslContexts() to set up CA trust stores and verification mode; (2) During TLS handshake, OpenSSL invokes customVerifyCallback; (3) doVerifyCertChain() performs X.509 chain verification, SAN matching, and certificate pinning; (4) For servers, ocspStapleAction() determines whether to attach OCSP responses; (5) OCSP responses are parsed using Asn1OcspUtility and validated for currency via OcspResponseWrapperImpl. This architecture ensures comprehensive certificate validation with flexible configuration and support for modern OCSP stapling security practices.\"\n}\n",
